## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the rate of change of concentration A with time t, which is the core of chemical kinetics rate laws. The physical relationship typically involves a function of A (the concentration-dependent rate) possibly modulated by explicit time dependence due to catalyst deactivation or external changes.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant rate, e.g., surface saturation)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive decay)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular elementary step)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (linear rate with intercept, approaching equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic logistic rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product catalysis, sigmoid growth)
- Time-dependent catalyst deactivation: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (exponentially decaying catalyst activity)
- Time power-law aging: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (gradual loss of activity following power law)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A + c3 * A**2) (excess substrate slows reaction)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood dual-site: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A)**2 (surface reaction requiring two adjacent sites)
- Power-law with time factor: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (separable time and concentration dependencies)
- Exponential autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A * (c2 - A) (accelerating autocatalysis)
- Generalized saturated kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + c3 * A)**c4 (fractional order with saturation)
- Product inhibition polynomial: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A - c2 * A**2 (polynomial rate from complex reversible mechanism)
- Double-sigmoid rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) - c3 * A (parallel pathways with saturation)
  ],
  
- heuristics": [
    "Constant rate over wide A range → zero‑order: dA_dt ≈ const
- Log‑log linearity between dA_dt and A → power‑law rate A^c1, indicating simple reaction order
- Exponential decay of dA_dt with time at fixed A → time‑dependent factor exp(‑c*t) times concentration term
- Rate exhibits a maximum as A decreases → autocatalytic multiplication A*(c ‑ A) captures sigmoidal conversion
- Rate increases then decreases with increasing A → substrate inhibition rational form A/(c1 + c2*A + c3*A^2)
- Linear A‑dependence with non‑zero intercept → reversible first‑order or constant source/sink: dA_dt = c0 + c1*A
- Rate trends show changing log‑log slope with A → fractional saturable form A^c1/(c2 + A^c1) or similar rational power‑law
- Separable time and concentration dependence → multiplicative combination f(t) * g(A), e.g., t**c * A**c1
- Rate asymptotically approaches zero like a power law at high A → dominant term A**c in denominator
- Initial lag phase followed by acceleration → rate involves increasing time factor, e.g., (c1 - exp(-c2*t)) * A

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
